# IMPORTANT: Use the existing PawnTrack files and the uploade…

> IMPORTANT: Use the existing PawnTrack files and the uploaded spreadsheet data.
>
> Build advanced financial forecasting dashboards using the real pawnshop data.
>
> Add:
>
> 1. Growth Dashboard
> - Total loans issued by week
> - Total loans issued by month
> - Growth percentage month-over-month
> - Total inventory growth
> - Total profit growth
> - Cash deployed trend
> - Cash recovered trend
>
> 2. Collections Dashboard
> - Amount due today
> - Amount due this week
> - Amount due next week
> - Amount overdue
> - Collection rate %
> - Recovery rate %
> - Expected collections calendar
>
> 3. Cash Forecast Dashboard
> - Expected cash inflow over next 7 days
> - Expected cash inflow over next 30 days
> - Expected cash inflow over next 90 days
> - Best case / likely case / worst case scenarios
>
> 4. Profit Forecast Dashboard
> Calculate:
> - Total principal outstanding
> - Total expected repayment
> - Expected interest income
> - Inventory value
> - Damaged/stolen losses
> - Expected net profit
>
> 5. Inventory Intelligence
> - Slow moving inventory
> - Inventory aging
> - Inventory value by category
> - Inventory turnover
> - Highest value items
> - Items to discount
>
> 6. Borrower Risk Scoring
> Create a score from:
> - overdue history
> - partial payments
> - missed payments
> - loan size
>
> Show:
> Green = low risk
> Orange = medium risk
> Red = high risk
>
> 7. Charts
> Use Recharts.
>
> Include:
> - Cashflow line chart
> - Profit line chart
> - Repayment forecast chart
> - Inventory category pie chart
> - Overdue borrower bar chart
> - Monthly growth chart
> - Collections trend chart
> - Profit forecast area chart
>
> 8. AI Analysis
> Use ChatGPT and Claude to analyze the synced Google Sheets data.
>
> Buttons:
> - Analyze Business
> - Forecast Next Month
> - Predict Cash Position
> - Identify Risky Clients
> - Recommend Collection Priorities
> - Recommend Inventory Discounts
>
> 9. Hands-Free Mode
> Voice commands must remain active continuously.
>
> Commands:
> "how much cash is due this week"
> "who owes me money"
> "show overdue loans"
> "show profit forecast"
> "show growth"
> "show inventory value"
> "what is my expected cash next week"
> "analyze business"

>
> Yes, it’s possible, but the clean way is through the official **WhatsApp Business Platform / Cloud API**, not by scraping the normal WhatsApp Business app.
>
> What it would look like:
>
> - Customer sends WhatsApp message to the business number.
> - Meta sends that message to our webhook in real time.
> - A PawnTrack bot reads it, extracts things like customer name, item, loan request, repayment promise, payment proof, phone number, due date, and risk notes.
> - It updates Google Sheets / PawnTrack automatically.
> - It replies using your business style, based on approved scripts and past message examples.
> - It hands off to you when the message is sensitive, angry, confusing, payment-related, or high-risk.
>
> Important caveat: WhatsApp allows automated replies, but business-initiated messages outside the 24-hour customer-service window need approved templates, and businesses need opt-in before messaging customers. Meta’s policy also says automation must have clear human escalation. For a pawnshop, we’d need to be especially careful around debt-collection wording because WhatsApp’s policy has restrictions around certain lending and debt collection uses.
>
> So yes: real-time intake and replies are very doable. The safest version is “assistant + human approval” for collections, and fully automatic for simple things like opening hours, item inquiry, loan status, repayment amount, due date reminders inside allowed rules, and inventory questions.
>
> I’m folding that WhatsApp idea into the “app-ready” path mentally, but I’ll keep today’s build focused on the forecasting dashboards you asked for. The dashboard can later receive WhatsApp events the same way it receives sheet data: through a small server that updates the business records and refreshes the views.

> ````text
> ## Additional Capabilities
> ### Browser Capabilities
> - `visibility`: Use to show or hide the browser to the user, and to determine the browser's current visibility. Keep browser work in the background unless the user asks to see it or live viewing is useful. When the browser should be visible, call set(true).
>   Read with `await (await browser.capabilities.get("visibility")).documentation()`.
> - `viewport`: Controls an explicit browser viewport override for responsive or device-size testing. Use it when a task calls for specific dimensions or breakpoint validation; otherwise leave it unset so the browser uses its normal 1280x720 viewport. Reset temporary overrides before finishing unless the user asked to keep them.
>   Read with `await (await browser.capabilities.get("viewport")).documentation()`.
> ### Tab Capabilities
> - `pageAssets`: List assets already observed in the current page state and bundle selected assets into a temporary local artifact.
>   Read with `await (await tab.capabilities.get("pageAssets")).documentation()`.
>
> ## Playwright
>
> Playwright is a critical part of the JavaScript API available to you.
>
> You only have access to a limited subset of the Playwright API, so only call functions that are explicitly defined.
> You do have access to `tab.playwright.evaluate(...)`, but only in a read-only page scope.
> Use locators for scoped interactions and targeted checks. For bulk DOM inspection, prefer one bounded read-only `evaluate(...)` that queries and projects the needed data. Avoid loops of locator property calls. In `evaluate(...)`, use basic DOM reads, limit returned elements, and do not assume globals or helpers such as `performance`, `NodeFilter`, `document.createTreeWalker`, or `FormData` exist.
>
> When using Playwright, keep and reuse a recent `tab.playwright.domSnapshot()` when it is available and you need it for locator construction or retry decisions. Treat the latest relevant snapshot as the source of truth for locator construction and retry decisions.
>
> ### Snapshot Discipline
>
> - Keep and reuse the latest relevant `domSnapshot()` until it proves stale or you need locator ground truth for UI that was not present in it.
> - Take a fresh `domSnapshot()` after navigation when you need to orient yourself or construct locators on the new page.
> - If a click times out, strict mode fails, or a selector parse error occurs, take a fresh `domSnapshot()` before forming the next locator.
> - Construct locators only from what appears in the latest snapshot. Do not guess labels, accessible names, or selectors.
> - Do not print full snapshot text repeatedly when a smaller excerpt, a `count()`, a specific attribute, or a direct locator check would answer the question with fewer tokens.
> - Do not discover page content by iterating through many results, cards, links, or rows and reading their text or attributes one by one.
> - Do not loop over a broad locator with `all()` and call `getAttribute(...)`, `textContent()`, or `innerText()` on each match. Each read crosses the browser boundary and becomes extremely expensive on large pages.
> - `locator.getAttribute(...)` is a single-element read, not a batch read. If the locator matches multiple elements, expect a strict-mode error rather than an array of attributes.
> - Use one broad observation to orient yourself: usually one fresh snapshot, or one screenshot if the visual structure is clearer than the DOM.
> - After that orientation step, narrow to the relevant section or a small number of strong candidates.
> - If the page is not getting narrower, do not scale up extraction across more elements. Change strategy instead.
> - Do not use `locator(...).allTextContents()`, `locator("body").textContent()`, or `locator("body").innerText()` as exploratory search tools across a page or large container.
> - Use broad text or attribute extraction only after you have already identified the exact container or element you need, and only when a smaller scoped check would not answer the question.
> - When you need many links, media URLs, or result titles, prefer a single `domSnapshot()` and parse the relevant lines, use the site's own search/filter UI, or navigate directly to a focused results page. Only fall back to per-element reads for a small, already-scoped set of candidates.
> - Do not use large body-text dumps, embedded app-state JSON such as `__NEXT_DATA__`, or repeated full-page extraction across multiple candidate pages as an exploratory search strategy.
> - Use large text or embedded JSON extraction only after you have already identified the relevant page, or when a site-specific skill explicitly depends on it.
>
> ### Hard Constraints For Playwright In This Runtime
>
> - Do not pass a regex as `name` to `getByRole(...)` in this environment. Use a plain string `name` only.
> - Do not use `.first()`, `.last()`, or `.nth()` unless you have just called `count()` on the same locator and explicitly confirmed why that position is correct.
> - Do not click, fill, or press on a locator until you have verified it resolves to exactly one element when uniqueness is not obvious.
> - Do not retry the same failing locator without a fresh `domSnapshot()`.
> - Do not use a guessed locator as an exploratory probe. If the latest snapshot does not clearly support the locator, do not spend timeout budget testing it.
> - Do not assume browser-side Playwright supports the full upstream API surface. If a method is not explicitly known to exist, do not call it.
> - Do not assume `locator(...).selectOption(...)` exists in this environment.
>
> ### Required Interaction Recipe
>
> Before every click, fill, select-like action, or press:
>
> 1. Reuse the latest relevant `domSnapshot()` when it still contains the locator ground truth you need. Take a fresh one only when it does not.
> 2. Build the most stable locator from the latest snapshot.
> 3. If uniqueness is not obvious from the selector itself, call `count()` on that locator.
> 4. Proceed only if the locator resolves to exactly one element.
> 5. Perform the action.
> 6. After the action, collect another observation only when the next decision requires it. Prefer a targeted state check when it answers the question; take a fresh snapshot when you need new locator ground truth.
>
> If `count()` is `0`:
>
> - The selector is wrong, stale, hidden, or the UI state is not ready.
> - Do not click anyway.
> - Do not wait on that locator to see if it eventually works.
> - Re-snapshot and rebuild the locator.
>
> If `count()` is greater than `1`:
>
> - The selector is ambiguous.
> - Scope to the correct container or switch to a stronger attribute.
> - Do not use `.first()` as a shortcut.
>
> ### Locator Strategy
>
> Build locators from what the snapshot actually shows, not what looks visually obvious.
>
> Prefer the most stable contract, in this order:
>
> 1. `data-testid`
> 2. Stable `data-*` attributes
> 3. Stable `href` (prefer exact or strong matches over broad substrings)
> 4. Scoped semantic role + accessible name using a string `name`
> 5. Scoped `getByText(...)`
> 6. Scoped CSS selectors via `locator(...)`
> 7. A scoped DOM-based click path or node-ID-based click when Playwright cannot produce a unique stable locator
>
> Use the most specific locator that is still durable.
>
> Treat a stable `href` as a strong hint, not proof of uniqueness. If multiple elements share the same `href`, scope to the correct card or container and confirm `count()` before clicking.
>
> Treat generic labels like `Menu`, `Main Menu`, `Help`, `Close`, `Default`, `Color`, `Size`, single-letter size labels such as `S`, `M`, `L`, `XL`, `Sort by`, `Search`, and `Add to cart` as ambiguous by default. Scope them to the correct container before acting.
>
> On search results, product grids, carousels, and modal-heavy pages, repeated `href`s and repeated generic labels are ambiguous by default. First identify the stable card or container, then scope the locator inside that container before clicking.
>
> ### Using `getByRole(..., { name })`
>
> - `name` is the accessible name, which may differ from visible text.
> - In the snapshot:
>   - `link "X"` usually reflects the accessible name.
>   - Nested text may be visible text only.
> - Use `getByRole` only when the accessible name is clearly present and likely unique in the latest snapshot.
>
> ### Interaction Best Practices
>
> - Scope before acting: find the right container or section first, then target the child element.
> - If you call `count()` on a locator, store the result in a local variable and reuse it unless the DOM changes.
> - Match the locator to the actual element type shown in the snapshot (link vs button vs menuitem vs generic text).
> - Do not assume every click navigates. If opening a menu or filter, wait for the expected UI state, not page load.
> - Prefer structured local signals such as selected control state, visible confirmation text, modal contents, a specific line item, or URL parameters over scraping broad result sections or dumping large parts of the page.
> - Do not add explicit `timeoutMs` to routine `click`, `fill`, `check`, or `setChecked` calls unless you have a concrete reason the target is slow to become actionable.
> - Reserve explicit timeout values for navigation, state transitions, or other known slow operations.
> - If you already know the exact destination URL and no click-side effect matters, prefer `tab.goto(url)` over a brittle locator click.
> - Do not reacquire `tab` inside each `node_repl` call. Reuse the existing `tab` binding to save tokens and preserve state. Only reacquire or reassign it when you intentionally switch tabs, after a kernel reset, or after a failed call that did not create the binding.
> - Do not use fixed sleeps as a default waiting strategy. After an action, prefer a concrete state check or targeted wait. Take a fresh snapshot when you need new locator ground truth.
> - If a fixed delay is truly unavoidable for a known transition, keep it short and follow it immediately with a specific verification step.
>
> ### Error Recovery
>
> - A strict mode violation means your locator is ambiguous.
> - Do not retry the same locator after a strict mode violation.
> - After strict mode fails, immediately inspect a fresh snapshot and rebuild the locator using tighter scope, a disambiguating container, or a stable attribute.
> - If a checkbox or radio exists but `check()` or `setChecked()` reports that it is hidden or did not change state, stop retrying the underlying input. Click its scoped visible associated `label[for]` or enclosing visible control once, then verify checked state.
> - A selector parse error means the locator syntax is invalid in this runtime.
> - Do not reuse the same locator form after a selector parse error.
> - A timeout usually means the target is missing, hidden, stale, offscreen, not yet rendered, or the selector is too broad.
> - Do not retry the same locator immediately after a timeout.
> - After a timeout, take a fresh snapshot, confirm the target still exists, and then either refine the locator or fall back to a more stable attribute.
> - If role or accessible-name targeting is unstable, fall back deliberately to a stable attribute (`data-*`, `href`, etc.), not brittle CSS structure.
> - If two locator attempts fail on the same target, stop escalating complexity on role or text locators. Switch to the most stable visible attribute from the snapshot or use a scoped DOM-based click path.
>
> ### Fallback Guidance
>
> - Prefer stable `href` values copied from the snapshot over guessed URL patterns.
> - Prefer scoped attribute selectors over global text selectors.
> - Use `getByText(...)` only when role-based or attribute-based locators are not reliable, and scope it to a container whenever possible.
> - Prefer attributes copied directly from the latest snapshot over inferred semantics, fragile CSS chains, or positional selectors.
> - Do not invent likely selectors. If the snapshot does not clearly expose a unique target, fetch a fresh snapshot and reassess before acting.
>
>
> ## API Reference
> Use this as the supported `agent.browsers.*` surface.
>
> ```ts
> // Installed by setupBrowserRuntime({ globals: globalThis }).
> const browser = await agent.browsers.get("iab");
> interface Agent {
>   browsers: Browsers; // API for finding and selecting browsers.
>   documentation: Documentation; // API for reading packaged browser-use documentation by name.
> }
>
> interface Browsers {
>   get(id: string): Promise<Browser>; // Get a browser by id or client type.
>   list(): Promise<Array<BrowserInfo>>; // List available browsers.
> }
>
> interface Browser {
>   browserId: string; // Browser id selected by `agent.browsers.get()`.
>   capabilities: BrowserCapabilityCollection; // Browser-scoped optional capabilities advertised by the connected backend; discover IDs with `await browser.capabilities.list()`, then call `await (await browser.capabilities.get(id)).documentation()` for method details.
>   tabs: Tabs; // API for interacting with browser tabs.
>   user: BrowserUser; // Readonly context about tabs in the user's browser windows.
>   documentation(): Promise<string>; // Read browser guidance and the core API reference.
>   nameSession(name: string): Promise<void>; // Name the current browser automation session.
> }
>
> interface BrowserUser {
>
>   openTabs(): Promise<Array<BrowserUserTabInfo>>; // List open top-level tabs across the user's browser windows ordered by `lastOpened` descending.
> }
>
> interface Tabs {
>
>   get(id: string): Promise<Tab>; // Get a tab by id.
>   list(): Promise<Array<TabInfo>>; // List open tabs in the browser.
>   new(): Promise<Tab>; // Create and return a new tab in the browser.
>   selected(): Promise<undefined | Tab>; // Return the currently selected tab, if any.
> }
>
> interface Tab {
>   capabilities: TabCapabilityCollection; // Tab-scoped optional capabilities advertised by the connected backend; discover IDs with `await tab.capabilities.list()`, then call `await (await tab.capabilities.get(id)).documentation()` for method details.
>   clipboard: TabClipboardAPI; // API for interacting with clipboard content in this tab.
>
>   cua: CUAAPI; // API for interacting with the tab via the cua api
>   dev: TabDevAPI; // API for developer-oriented tab inspection.
>   dom_cua: DomCUAAPI; // API for interacting with the tab via the dom based cua api
>   id: string; // A tab's unique identifier
>   playwright: PlaywrightAPI; // API for interacting with the tab via the playwright api
>   back(): Promise<void>; // Navigate this tab back in history.
>   close(): Promise<void>; // Close this tab.
>   forward(): Promise<void>; // Navigate this tab forward in history.
>   goto(url: string): Promise<void>; // Open a URL in this tab.
>   reload(): Promise<void>; // Reload this tab.
>   screenshot(options: ScreenshotOptions): Promise<Uint8Array>; // Capture a screenshot of this tab.
>   title(): Promise<undefined | string>; // Get the current title for this tab.
>   url(): Promise<undefined | string>; // Get the current URL for this tab.
> }
>
> interface CUAAPI {
>   click(options: ClickOptions): Promise<void>; // Click at a coordinate in the current viewport.
>   double_click(options: DoubleClickOptions): Promise<void>; // Double click at a coordinate in the current viewport.
>   
>   drag(options: DragOptions): Promise<void>; // Drag from a point to a point by the provided path.
>   keypress(options: KeypressOptions): Promise<void>; // Press control characters at the current focused element (focus it first via click/dblclick).
>   move(options: MoveOptions): Promise<void>; // Move the mouse to a point by the provided x and y coordinates.
>   scroll(options: ScrollOptions): Promise<void>; // Scroll by a delta from a specific viewport coordinate.
>   type(options: TypeOptions): Promise<void>; // Type text at the current focus.
> }
>
> interface DomCUAAPI {
>   click(options: DomClickOptions): Promise<void>; // Click a DOM node by its id from the visible DOM snapshot.
>   double_click(options: DomClickOptions): Promise<void>; // Double-click a DOM node by its id.
>   
>   get_visible_dom(): Promise<unknown>; // Return a filtered DOM with node ids for interactable elements.
>   keypress(options: DomKeypressOptions): Promise<void>; // Press control characters at the currently focused element (focus it first via click/dblclick).
>   scroll(options: DomScrollOptions): Promise<void>; // Scroll either the page or a specific node (if node_id provided) by deltas.
>   type(options: DomTypeOptions): Promise<void>; // Type text into the currently focused element (focus via click first).
> }
>
> interface PlaywrightAPI {
>   domSnapshot(): Promise<string>; // Return a snapshot of the current DOM as a string, including expanded iframe body content when available.
>
>   evaluate<TResult, TArg>(pageFunction: PlaywrightEvaluateFunction<TArg, TResult>, arg?: TArg, options?: PlaywrightEvaluateOptions): Promise<TResult>; // Evaluate JavaScript in a read-only page scope.
>   expectNavigation<T>(action: () => Promise<T>, options: { timeoutMs?: number; url?: string; waitUntil?: LoadState }): Promise<T>; // Expect a navigation triggered by an action.
>   frameLocator(frameSelector: string): PlaywrightFrameLocator; // Create a frame-scoped locator builder.
>   getByLabel(text: TextMatcher, options: { exact?: boolean }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by label text within the page.
>   getByPlaceholder(text: TextMatcher, options: { exact?: boolean }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by placeholder text within the page.
>   getByRole(role: string, options: { exact?: boolean; name?: TextMatcher }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by ARIA role within the page.
>   getByTestId(testId: string): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by test id within the page.
>   getByText(text: TextMatcher, options: { exact?: boolean }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by text within the page.
>   locator(selector: string): PlaywrightLocator; // Create a locator scoped to this tab.
>   waitForEvent(event: "download", options?: WaitForEventOptions): Promise<PlaywrightDownload>; // Wait for the next event on the page.
>
>   waitForLoadState(options: PageWaitForLoadStateOptions): Promise<void>; // Wait for the page to reach a specific load state.
>   waitForTimeout(timeoutMs: number): Promise<void>; // Wait for a fixed duration.
>   waitForURL(url: string, options: PageWaitForURLOptions): Promise<void>; // Wait for the page URL to match the provided value.
> }
>
> interface PlaywrightFrameLocator {
>   frameLocator(frameSelector: string): PlaywrightFrameLocator; // Create a locator scoped to a nested frame.
>   getByLabel(text: TextMatcher, options: { exact?: boolean }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by label within this frame.
>   getByPlaceholder(text: TextMatcher, options: { exact?: boolean }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by placeholder within this frame.
>   getByRole(role: string, options: { exact?: boolean; name?: TextMatcher }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by ARIA role within this frame.
>   getByTestId(testId: string): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by test id within this frame.
>   getByText(text: TextMatcher, options: { exact?: boolean }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by text within this frame.
>   locator(selector: string): PlaywrightLocator; // Create a locator scoped to this frame.
> }
>
> interface PlaywrightLocator {
>   all(): Promise<Array<PlaywrightLocator>>; // Resolve to a list of locators for each matched element.
>   allTextContents(options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<Array<string>>; // Return `textContent` for *all* elements matched by this locator.
>   and(locator: PlaywrightLocator): PlaywrightLocator; // Return a locator matching elements that satisfy both this locator and `locator`.
>   check(options: LocatorCheckOptions): Promise<void>; // Check a checkbox or switch-like control.
>   click(options: LocatorClickOptions): Promise<void>; // Click the element matched by this locator.
>   count(): Promise<number>; // Number of elements matching this locator.
>   dblclick(options: LocatorClickOptions): Promise<void>; // Double-click the element matched by this locator.
>
>   fill(value: string, options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<void>; // Replace the element's value with the provided text.
>   filter(options: LocatorFilterOptions): PlaywrightLocator; // Narrow this locator by additional constraints.
>   first(): PlaywrightLocator; // Return a locator pointing at the first matched element.
>   getAttribute(name: string, options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<null | string>; // Return an attribute value from the first matched element.
>   getByLabel(text: TextMatcher, options: { exact?: boolean }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by label text, scoped to this locator.
>   getByPlaceholder(text: TextMatcher, options: { exact?: boolean }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by placeholder text, scoped to this locator.
>   getByRole(role: string, options: { exact?: boolean; name?: TextMatcher }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by ARIA role, scoped to this locator.
>   getByTestId(testId: string): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by test id, scoped to this locator.
>   getByText(text: TextMatcher, options: { exact?: boolean }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by text content, scoped to this locator.
>   innerText(options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<string>; // Return the rendered (visible) text of the first matched element.
>   isEnabled(): Promise<boolean>; // Whether the first matched element is currently enabled.
>   isVisible(): Promise<boolean>; // Whether the first matched element is currently visible.
>   last(): PlaywrightLocator; // Return a locator pointing at the last matched element.
>   locator(selector: string, options: LocatorLocatorOptions): PlaywrightLocator; // Create a descendant locator scoped to this locator.
>   nth(index: number): PlaywrightLocator; // Return a locator pointing at the Nth matched element.
>   or(locator: PlaywrightLocator): PlaywrightLocator; // Return a locator matching elements that satisfy either this locator or `locator`.
>   press(value: string, options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<void>; // Press a keyboard key while this locator is focused.
>   selectOption(value: SelectOptionInput | Array<SelectOptionInput>, options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<void>; // Select one or more options on a native `<select>` element.
>   setChecked(checked: boolean, options: LocatorCheckOptions): Promise<void>; // Set a checkbox or switch-like control to a checked/unchecked state.
>   textContent(options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<null | string>; // Return the raw textContent of the first matched element (or null if missing).
>   type(value: string, options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<void>; // Type text into the element without clearing existing content.
>   uncheck(options: LocatorCheckOptions): Promise<void>; // Uncheck a checkbox or switch-like control.
>   waitFor(options: LocatorWaitForOptions): Promise<void>; // Wait for the element to reach a specific state.
> }

> ````text
> ## Additional Capabilities
> ### Browser Capabilities
> - `visibility`: Use to show or hide the browser to the user, and to determine the browser's current visibility. Keep browser work in the background unless the user asks to see it or live viewing is useful. When the browser should be visible, call set(true).
>   Read with `await (await browser.capabilities.get("visibility")).documentation()`.
> - `viewport`: Controls an explicit browser viewport override for responsive or device-size testing. Use it when a task calls for specific dimensions or breakpoint validation; otherwise leave it unset so the browser uses its normal 1280x720 viewport. Reset temporary overrides before finishing unless the user asked to keep them.
>   Read with `await (await browser.capabilities.get("viewport")).documentation()`.
> ### Tab Capabilities
> - `pageAssets`: List assets already observed in the current page state and bundle selected assets into a temporary local artifact.
>   Read with `await (await tab.capabilities.get("pageAssets")).documentation()`.
>
> ## Playwright
>
> Playwright is a critical part of the JavaScript API available to you.
>
> You only have access to a limited subset of the Playwright API, so only call functions that are explicitly defined.
> You do have access to `tab.playwright.evaluate(...)`, but only in a read-only page scope.
> Use locators for scoped interactions and targeted checks. For bulk DOM inspection, prefer one bounded read-only `evaluate(...)` that queries and projects the needed data. Avoid loops of locator property calls. In `evaluate(...)`, use basic DOM reads, limit returned elements, and do not assume globals or helpers such as `performance`, `NodeFilter`, `document.createTreeWalker`, or `FormData` exist.
>
> When using Playwright, keep and reuse a recent `tab.playwright.domSnapshot()` when it is available and you need it for locator construction or retry decisions. Treat the latest relevant snapshot as the source of truth for locator construction and retry decisions.
>
> ### Snapshot Discipline
>
> - Keep and reuse the latest relevant `domSnapshot()` until it proves stale or you need locator ground truth for UI that was not present in it.
> - Take a fresh `domSnapshot()` after navigation when you need to orient yourself or construct locators on the new page.
> - If a click times out, strict mode fails, or a selector parse error occurs, take a fresh `domSnapshot()` before forming the next locator.
> - Construct locators only from what appears in the latest snapshot. Do not guess labels, accessible names, or selectors.
> - Do not print full snapshot text repeatedly when a smaller excerpt, a `count()`, a specific attribute, or a direct locator check would answer the question with fewer tokens.
> - Do not discover page content by iterating through many results, cards, links, or rows and reading their text or attributes one by one.
> - Do not loop over a broad locator with `all()` and call `getAttribute(...)`, `textContent()`, or `innerText()` on each match. Each read crosses the browser boundary and becomes extremely expensive on large pages.
> - `locator.getAttribute(...)` is a single-element read, not a batch read. If the locator matches multiple elements, expect a strict-mode error rather than an array of attributes.
> - Use one broad observation to orient yourself: usually one fresh snapshot, or one screenshot if the visual structure is clearer than the DOM.
> - After that orientation step, narrow to the relevant section or a small number of strong candidates.
> - If the page is not getting narrower, do not scale up extraction across more elements. Change strategy instead.
> - Do not use `locator(...).allTextContents()`, `locator("body").textContent()`, or `locator("body").innerText()` as exploratory search tools across a page or large container.
> - Use broad text or attribute extraction only after you have already identified the exact container or element you need, and only when a smaller scoped check would not answer the question.
> - When you need many links, media URLs, or result titles, prefer a single `domSnapshot()` and parse the relevant lines, use the site's own search/filter UI, or navigate directly to a focused results page. Only fall back to per-element reads for a small, already-scoped set of candidates.
> - Do not use large body-text dumps, embedded app-state JSON such as `__NEXT_DATA__`, or repeated full-page extraction across multiple candidate pages as an exploratory search strategy.
> - Use large text or embedded JSON extraction only after you have already identified the relevant page, or when a site-specific skill explicitly depends on it.
>
> ### Hard Constraints For Playwright In This Runtime
>
> - Do not pass a regex as `name` to `getByRole(...)` in this environment. Use a plain string `name` only.
> - Do not use `.first()`, `.last()`, or `.nth()` unless you have just called `count()` on the same locator and explicitly confirmed why that position is correct.
> - Do not click, fill, or press on a locator until you have verified it resolves to exactly one element when uniqueness is not obvious.
> - Do not retry the same failing locator without a fresh `domSnapshot()`.
> - Do not use a guessed locator as an exploratory probe. If the latest snapshot does not clearly support the locator, do not spend timeout budget testing it.
> - Do not assume browser-side Playwright supports the full upstream API surface. If a method is not explicitly known to exist, do not call it.
> - Do not assume `locator(...).selectOption(...)` exists in this environment.
>
> ### Required Interaction Recipe
>
> Before every click, fill, select-like action, or press:
>
> 1. Reuse the latest relevant `domSnapshot()` when it still contains the locator ground truth you need. Take a fresh one only when it does not.
> 2. Build the most stable locator from the latest snapshot.
> 3. If uniqueness is not obvious from the selector itself, call `count()` on that locator.
> 4. Proceed only if the locator resolves to exactly one element.
> 5. Perform the action.
> 6. After the action, collect another observation only when the next decision requires it. Prefer a targeted state check when it answers the question; take a fresh snapshot when you need new locator ground truth.
>
> If `count()` is `0`:
>
> - The selector is wrong, stale, hidden, or the UI state is not ready.
> - Do not click anyway.
> - Do not wait on that locator to see if it eventually works.
> - Re-snapshot and rebuild the locator.
>
> If `count()` is greater than `1`:
>
> - The selector is ambiguous.
> - Scope to the correct container or switch to a stronger attribute.
> - Do not use `.first()` as a shortcut.
>
> ### Locator Strategy
>
> Build locators from what the snapshot actually shows, not what looks visually obvious.
>
> Prefer the most stable contract, in this order:
>
> 1. `data-testid`
> 2. Stable `data-*` attributes
> 3. Stable `href` (prefer exact or strong matches over broad substrings)
> 4. Scoped semantic role + accessible name using a string `name`
> 5. Scoped `getByText(...)`
> 6. Scoped CSS selectors via `locator(...)`
> 7. A scoped DOM-based click path or node-ID-based click when Playwright cannot produce a unique stable locator
>
> Use the most specific locator that is still durable.
>
> Treat a stable `href` as a strong hint, not proof of uniqueness. If multiple elements share the same `href`, scope to the correct card or container and confirm `count()` before clicking.
>
> Treat generic labels like `Menu`, `Main Menu`, `Help`, `Close`, `Default`, `Color`, `Size`, single-letter size labels such as `S`, `M`, `L`, `XL`, `Sort by`, `Search`, and `Add to cart` as ambiguous by default. Scope them to the correct container before acting.
>
> On search results, product grids, carousels, and modal-heavy pages, repeated `href`s and repeated generic labels are ambiguous by default. First identify the stable card or container, then scope the locator inside that container before clicking.
>
> ### Using `getByRole(..., { name })`
>
> - `name` is the accessible name, which may differ from visible text.
> - In the snapshot:
>   - `link "X"` usually reflects the accessible name.
>   - Nested text may be visible text only.
> - Use `getByRole` only when the accessible name is clearly present and likely unique in the latest snapshot.
>
> ### Interaction Best Practices
>
> - Scope before acting: find the right container or section first, then target the child element.
> - If you call `count()` on a locator, store the result in a local variable and reuse it unless the DOM changes.
> - Match the locator to the actual element type shown in the snapshot (link vs button vs menuitem vs generic text).
> - Do not assume every click navigates. If opening a menu or filter, wait for the expected UI state, not page load.
> - Prefer structured local signals such as selected control state, visible confirmation text, modal contents, a specific line item, or URL parameters over scraping broad result sections or dumping large parts of the page.
> - Do not add explicit `timeoutMs` to routine `click`, `fill`, `check`, or `setChecked` calls unless you have a concrete reason the target is slow to become actionable.
> - Reserve explicit timeout values for navigation, state transitions, or other known slow operations.
> - If you already know the exact destination URL and no click-side effect matters, prefer `tab.goto(url)` over a brittle locator click.
> - Do not reacquire `tab` inside each `node_repl` call. Reuse the existing `tab` binding to save tokens and preserve state. Only reacquire or reassign it when you intentionally switch tabs, after a kernel reset, or after a failed call that did not create the binding.
> - Do not use fixed sleeps as a default waiting strategy. After an action, prefer a concrete state check or targeted wait. Take a fresh snapshot when you need new locator ground truth.
> - If a fixed delay is truly unavoidable for a known transition, keep it short and follow it immediately with a specific verification step.
>
> ### Error Recovery
>
> - A strict mode violation means your locator is ambiguous.
> - Do not retry the same locator after a strict mode violation.
> - After strict mode fails, immediately inspect a fresh snapshot and rebuild the locator using tighter scope, a disambiguating container, or a stable attribute.
> - If a checkbox or radio exists but `check()` or `setChecked()` reports that it is hidden or did not change state, stop retrying the underlying input. Click its scoped visible associated `label[for]` or enclosing visible control once, then verify checked state.
> - A selector parse error means the locator syntax is invalid in this runtime.
> - Do not reuse the same locator form after a selector parse error.
> - A timeout usually means the target is missing, hidden, stale, offscreen, not yet rendered, or the selector is too broad.
> - Do not retry the same locator immediately after a timeout.
> - After a timeout, take a fresh snapshot, confirm the target still exists, and then either refine the locator or fall back to a more stable attribute.
> - If role or accessible-name targeting is unstable, fall back deliberately to a stable attribute (`data-*`, `href`, etc.), not brittle CSS structure.
> - If two locator attempts fail on the same target, stop escalating complexity on role or text locators. Switch to the most stable visible attribute from the snapshot or use a scoped DOM-based click path.
>
> ### Fallback Guidance
>
> - Prefer stable `href` values copied from the snapshot over guessed URL patterns.
> - Prefer scoped attribute selectors over global text selectors.
> - Use `getByText(...)` only when role-based or attribute-based locators are not reliable, and scope it to a container whenever possible.
> - Prefer attributes copied directly from the latest snapshot over inferred semantics, fragile CSS chains, or positional selectors.
> - Do not invent likely selectors. If the snapshot does not clearly expose a unique target, fetch a fresh snapshot and reassess before acting.
>
>

> interface PlaywrightLocator {

>   getByPlaceholder(text: TextMatcher, options: { exact?: boolean }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by placeholder text, scoped to this locator.
>   getByRole(role: string, options: { exact?: boolean; name?: TextMatcher }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by ARIA role, scoped to this locator.
>   getByTestId(testId: string): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by test id, scoped to this locator.
>   getByText(text: TextMatcher, options: { exact?: boolean }): PlaywrightLocator; // Find elements by text content, scoped to this locator.
>   innerText(options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<string>; // Return the rendered (visible) text of the first matched element.
>   isEnabled(): Promise<boolean>; // Whether the first matched element is currently enabled.
>   isVisible(): Promise<boolean>; // Whether the first matched element is currently visible.
>   last(): PlaywrightLocator; // Return a locator pointing at the last matched element.
>   locator(selector: string, options: LocatorLocatorOptions): PlaywrightLocator; // Create a descendant locator scoped to this locator.
>   nth(index: number): PlaywrightLocator; // Return a locator pointing at the Nth matched element.
>   or(locator: PlaywrightLocator): PlaywrightLocator; // Return a locator matching elements that satisfy either this locator or `locator`.
>   press(value: string, options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<void>; // Press a keyboard key while this locator is focused.
>   selectOption(value: SelectOptionInput | Array<SelectOptionInput>, options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<void>; // Select one or more options on a native `<select>` element.
>   setChecked(checked: boolean, options: LocatorCheckOptions): Promise<void>; // Set a checkbox or switch-like control to a checked/unchecked state.
>   textContent(options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<null | string>; // Return the raw textContent of the first matched element (or null if missing).
>   type(value: string, options: { timeoutMs?: number }): Promise<void>; // Type text into the element without clearing existing content.
>   uncheck(options: LocatorCheckOptions): Promise<void>; // Uncheck a checkbox or switch-like control.
>   waitFor(options: LocatorWaitForOptions): Promise<void>; // Wait for the element to reach a specific state.

> The browser connection is back. I’m checking whether the preview server is still alive; if it isn’t, I’ll start a fresh one and navigate the in-app browser to it.

> MCP tool call

> node_repl.js

That message means: the app can calculate the sale now, but it cannot write to **NEW ONE** until the backend has permission to edit your Google Sheet.

Do this:

1. In Google Cloud, create a service account.
2. Enable the Google Sheets API for that project.
3. Create/download a JSON key for the service account.
4. Open **NEW ONE** in Google Sheets.
5. Share the sheet with the service account email as **Editor**.
6. Start the backend with that JSON key:

```powershell
$env:GOOGLE_SERVICE_ACCOUNT_JSON='PASTE_THE_SERVICE_ACCOUNT_JSON_HERE'
node .\pawntrack-ai-bridge.mjs
```

Then `Mark Inventory Sold` will update **NEW ONE** directly:
- `Listed on Market place` → `Sold`
- `Amount paid` → pawned amount
- `Sell amount` → sale price
- `Profit/loss` → sale price minus pawned amount

Google’s docs confirm that service accounts are the right server-side identity pattern, and Sheets writes use the `spreadsheets.values.batchUpdate` endpoint. Sources: [Google service accounts](https://cloud.google.com/iam/docs/service-accounts-create), [Sheets batchUpdate](https://developers.google.com/sheets/api/reference/rest/v4/spreadsheets.values/batchUpdate).

Yes, step 3 is the JSON key download.

Do this:

1. Open [Google Cloud Service Accounts](https://console.cloud.google.com/iam-admin/serviceaccounts).
2. Select your Google Cloud project.
3. Click the service account email you created.
4. Click the **Keys** tab.
5. Click **Add key**.
6. Choose **Create new key**.
7. Select **JSON**.
8. Click **Create**.

A `.json` file will download to your computer. Keep it safe and don’t send it in chat. Google says the key file downloads only once, so save it somewhere you can find again.

After that, open the JSON file and copy the `client_email`. Share the **NEW ONE** Google Sheet with that email as **Editor**.

Source: [Google Cloud service account key docs](https://docs.cloud.google.com/iam/docs/keys-create-delete).

> Plan
>
> # Firestore Primary Database Plan
>
> ## Summary
> Replace the current PostgreSQL mirror with **Cloud Firestore as the primary database** for PawnTrack, while keeping the Flutter app’s existing backend API shape. The backend remains the only component with Firebase credentials. Google Sheets becomes a synced secondary record, not the source of truth.
>
> Use the existing Firebase/Google project and seed Firestore once from the current `NEW ONE` Google Sheet.
>
> ## Key Changes
>
> ### Backend
> - Replace `googleSheetsPostgresBridge.mjs` with a Firestore-backed bridge, preferably named `googleSheetsFirestoreBridge.mjs`.
> - Remove `pg` and `DATABASE_URL`; add `firebase-admin` and a multipart parser such as `busboy`.
> - Update config to support:
>   - `firebaseProjectId`
>   - `firebaseServiceAccountFile` or `firebaseServiceAccountJson`
>   - `firebaseStorageBucket`
>   - `firestoreDatabaseId`, default `(default)`
>   - existing Google Sheets config
> - Initialize Firebase Admin SDK server-side only.
> - Firestore collections:
>   - `customers`
>   - `loans`
>   - `items`
>   - `repayments`
>   - `inventory`
>   - `sales`
>   - `riskScores`
>   - `staffUsers`
>   - `auditLog`
>   - `whatsappMessages`
>   - `voiceCommands`
>   - `syncJobs`
>   - `sheetSnapshots`
> - Add Cloud Storage upload support for:
>   - customer photo
>   - ID photo
>   - item photos
>   - proof-of-ownership files
> - Storage paths:
>   - `customers/{customerId}/customer-photo/{fileId}`
>   - `customers/{customerId}/id-photo/{fileId}`
>   - `items/{itemId}/photos/{fileId}`
>   - `items/{itemId}/proof/{fileId}`
>
> ### Data Flow
> - Add an idempotent `POST /api/import/sheets-to-firestore` endpoint.
>   - Reads current Google Sheets.
>   - Upserts Firestore docs using stable IDs like `active-pawns-row-{rowNumber}` and `company-owned-row-{rowNumber}`.
>   - Records import status in `syncJobs`.
> - Keep compatible Flutter endpoints:
>   - `GET /api/sheet-data`
>   - `POST /api/sheet-batch-update`
>   - `POST /api/inventory-sale`
> - Change those endpoints internally:
>   - Write Firestore first.
>   - Create a `syncJobs` record for the matching Google Sheets update.
>   - Attempt Google Sheets sync.
>   - Mark sync job `synced` or `failed`.
> - `GET /api/sheet-data` should return the same payload shape Flutter expects, but sourced from Firestore after import.
>
> ### Flutter
> - Keep `PawnTrackApi` as an HTTP backend client.
> - Do not add FlutterFire for Firestore in this phase.
> - Add file upload methods to the API client:
>   - `uploadCustomerPhoto`
>   - `uploadIdPhoto`
>   - `uploadItemPhoto`
>   - `uploadProofOfOwnership`
> - Add an image picker/file picker package for web/mobile uploads.
> - Store returned Cloud Storage URLs in Firestore records and mirror URL fields to Google Sheets where relevant.
>
> ### Docs
> - Replace PostgreSQL setup docs with Firebase setup docs.
> - Explain required Firebase IAM:
>   - Firestore read/write access
>   - Cloud Storage object read/write access
>   - existing Google Sheets access
> - Keep Google Sheets credential guidance, but remove Postgres database setup.
>
> ## Test Plan
> - Run backend syntax check and startup health check.
> - Verify Firebase Admin connects using existing project credentials.
> - Run one-time import from Google Sheets and confirm Firestore collections are populated.
> - Verify `GET /api/sheet-data` returns the same shape Flutter currently expects.
> - Create new pawn:
>   - Firestore loan/customer/item records created.
>   - Google Sheet row synced.
>   - Audit log written.
> - Record repayment and extension:
>   - Firestore updated first.
>   - Repayment record created.
>   - Sheet update sync job succeeds.
> - Move forfeited item to inventory and mark item sold:
>   - Inventory/sales records updated.
>   - Actual profit calculated.
>   - Sheet updated.
> - Upload customer, ID, item, and proof photos:
>   - Files saved to Cloud Storage.
>   - URLs stored in Firestore.
> - Simulate Google Sheets failure:
>   - Firestore write still succeeds.
>   - Sync job is marked failed and retryable.
>
> ## Assumptions
> - Backend-owned Firebase is the target architecture.
> - Firestore is the primary source of truth.
> - Google Sheets remains a secondary synced business record.
> - Existing Firebase/Google project will be used.
> - Existing service account can be reused if it has Firestore and Storage permissions; otherwise IAM must be updated.
> - Flutter will not talk directly to Firestore in this phase.
> - Cloud Storage is included now for photos/files.
>
> Sources: Firebase Admin SDK setup, Cloud Firestore quickstart, and Cloud Storage Admin docs:  
> https://firebase.google.com/docs/admin/setup  
> https://firebase.google.com/docs/firestore/quickstart  
> https://firebase.google.com/docs/storage/admin/start
</details>

> # Host PawnTrack on Firebase Hosting with Cloud Run API
>
> ## Summary
> Deploy the Flutter web app to Firebase Hosting for project `lastresort-2b8b1`, and deploy the existing Node backend as a Cloud Run service named `pawntrack-api`. Firebase Hosting will serve the app at `https://lastresort-2b8b1.web.app` and proxy `/api/**` requests to Cloud Run so the hosted app can use Firestore, Google Sheets sync, uploads, and sales/repayment actions.
>
> ## Key Changes
> - Update Flutter API base URL logic so production uses same-origin `/api`, while local development still falls back to `http://127.0.0.1:8805`.
> - Add Firebase Hosting config in `pawntrack-flutter-port/app/firebase.json`:
>   - `public`: `build/web`
>   - rewrite `/api/**` to Cloud Run service `pawntrack-api` in `europe-west1`
>   - rewrite all other paths to `/index.html` for Flutter routing.
> - Add `.firebaserc` in the Flutter app folder with default project `lastresort-2b8b1`.
> - Deploy backend with Cloud Run using the existing Node server:
>   - Service name: `pawntrack-api`
>   - Region: `europe-west1`
>   - Public invoker for now, because login will be added later.
>   - Environment: `FIREBASE_PROJECT_ID`, `FIREBASE_STORAGE_BUCKET`, `FIRESTORE_DATABASE_ID`, `GOOGLE_SHEET_ID`.
>   - Secret: existing service-account JSON stored in Secret Manager and mounted as both `GOOGLE_SERVICE_ACCOUNT_JSON` and `FIREBASE_SERVICE_ACCOUNT_JSON`.
> - Build and deploy:
>   - `flutter build web`
>   - deploy Cloud Run backend
>   - `firebase deploy --only hosting --project lastresort-2b8b1`
>
> ## Test Plan
> - Verify backend before Hosting:
>   - Cloud Run `/api/health` returns Firestore, Storage, and Google Sheets as healthy.
>   - Cloud Run `/api/sheet-data` returns active pawns, OS debts, inventory, and damaged goods.
> - Verify Hosting:
>   - `https://lastresort-2b8b1.web.app` loads the Flutter app.
>   - `https://lastresort-2b8b1.web.app/api/health` routes through Hosting to Cloud Run.
>   - App dashboard loads Firestore-backed data without `127.0.0.1`.
> - Verify key workflows:
>   - create/read a test pawn or controlled update only if you approve a real data write
>   - upload path still saves to Cloud Storage
>   - Google Sheets sync jobs are created after backend writes.
> - Verify browser behavior:
>   - hard refresh works
>   - direct navigation to app routes serves Flutter, not a 404.
>
> ## Assumptions
> - Use Firebase Hosting classic, not Firebase App Hosting, because this is a static Flutter web app.
> - Use Cloud Run, not Cloud Functions, because the current backend is already a normal Node HTTP server.
> - Use `europe-west1` because Firebase Hosting officially supports Cloud Run rewrites there; `africa-south1` is not listed for Hosting rewrites.
> - The first hosted release is public-link accessible; Firebase Auth/password protection is a follow-up before real production use.
> - References: [Firebase Hosting quickstart](https://firebase.google.com/docs/hosting/quickstart), [Firebase Hosting rewrites to Cloud Run](https://firebase.google.com/docs/hosting/full-config).

Short answer: **not by making a port**.

Firebase Hosting does not expose your local port like `8805` or `8814`. Once the app is hosted, it runs on:

`https://lastresort-2b8b1.web.app`

and it can only call:

- static files on Firebase Hosting
- Firebase client SDKs like Firestore/Auth/Storage
- a public backend URL
- a Hosting rewrite to Cloud Run/Functions, which needs billing

So without billing, we have two realistic paths:

1. **Static Firebase Hosting only**
   - Works without billing on Spark plan.
   - The Flutter app can be hosted.
   - But the current backend API at `127.0.0.1:8805` will not work online.
   - We would need to change the app to talk directly to Firestore with FlutterFire.

2. **Full working app with backend**
   - Needs Cloud Run or Functions.
   - Requires billing/Blaze because Cloud Run, Cloud Build, Artifact Registry, and Secret Manager are not available on Spark for this use.

Best no-billing workaround: **make a Firebase Hosting-only version that reads/writes Firestore directly from Flutter**. It can show the dashboard, active pawns, inventory, reports, etc. But Google Sheets sync and secure service-account-only operations would need to wait until billing/backend is enabled.

Firebase pricing confirms Hosting has Spark/no-payment support, while Cloud Run/App Hosting related Google Cloud products are not available on Spark: [Firebase pricing](https://firebase.google.com/pricing).

> how do we change the app to talk directly to Firestore with FlutterFire? What exactly is being hosted at 127.0.0.1:8805 and what is its point?

<details><summary>1 previous message</summary>

> I’ll map this to your actual code so the answer is concrete: what the `8805` server does today, what Flutter is calling, and what would move into FlutterFire if we remove that server for Firebase Hosting.
</details>

Yes. For **no billing**, the clean move is:

1. Host only the Flutter web app on Firebase Hosting.
2. Remove the need for `/api/...` calls.
3. Let Flutter talk directly to Firestore and Storage using FlutterFire.

**What `127.0.0.1:8805` Is**
`127.0.0.1:8805` is your **local Node backend API server**, not the website.

It is running this backend file:

[pawntrack-flutter-port/server/googleSheetsFirestoreBridge.mjs](./pawntrack-flutter-port/server/googleSheetsFirestoreBridge.mjs:1)

Its point is to safely do things the Flutter app should not do directly:

- Use the Firebase Admin SDK with the service account.
- Read from the Google Sheet.
- Import Google Sheets rows into Firestore.
- Return `/api/sheet-data` to Flutter.
- Write updates to Firestore first.
- Create `syncJobs` for Google Sheets sync.
- Upload photos/files to Cloud Storage.
- Keep service-account credentials off the client app.

The Flutter app currently calls it from:

[pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/services/pawntrack_api.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/services/pawntrack_api.dart:8)

Examples:

- `GET /api/sheet-data`
- `POST /api/sheet-batch-update`
- `POST /api/inventory-sale`
- `POST /api/upload/...`

**Why It Won’t Work on Firebase Hosting**
When hosted at:

`https://lastresort-2b8b1.web.app`

the browser cannot use `127.0.0.1:8805`, because that means “the user’s own computer”, not your Codex/backend machine.

Firebase Hosting also cannot expose your local port to the internet. To keep the backend, we need Cloud Run or Functions, and those require billing.

**How To Change The App To Use Firestore Directly**
We would replace `PawnTrackApi` with a FlutterFire data service.

Main changes:

- Add packages:
  - `cloud_firestore`
  - `firebase_storage`
  - later: `firebase_auth`

- Read dashboard data directly from Firestore:
  - easiest first step: read `sheetSnapshots/latest`
  - parse `payloadJson`
  - keep returning `SheetSource` so the UI does not need a big rewrite.

- Later, move screens to real collections:
  - `customers`
  - `loans`
  - `items`
  - `repayments`
  - `inventory`
  - `sales`
  - `riskScores`

- Replace uploads:
  - use `firebase_storage` directly from Flutter
  - write returned download URLs into Firestore.

- Add Firestore/Storage security rules:
  - for testing, locked to signed-in users
  - for real use, staff-only access with Firebase Auth.

**What We Lose Without The Backend**
Direct FlutterFire can do Firestore and Storage, but it cannot safely do these:

- Google Sheets sync using service-account credentials
- server-side audit enforcement
- secure AI/voice backend commands
- server-side WhatsApp sending
- trusted profit/risk calculations that users cannot tamper with

So the no-billing version can be a working Firebase-hosted pawnshop app, but Google Sheets sync becomes manual or delayed until Cloud Run is available.

Best path: make a **Hosting-only FlutterFire version now**, using Firestore as the live database. Keep the Node backend files for later Cloud Run deployment when billing is enabled.

> make a Hosting-only FlutterFire version now, using Firestore as the live database. Keep the Node backend files for later Cloud Run deployment when billing is enabled.

I tried to enable Anonymous Auth programmatically, but Google returned:

`BILLING_NOT_ENABLED: Identity Platform feature requires billing to be enabled`

So for the no-billing route, you need to initialize Firebase Authentication manually in the Firebase Console.

Open this:

[Firebase Authentication for lastresort-2b8b1](https://console.firebase.google.com/project/lastresort-2b8b1/authentication/providers)

Then:

1. Click **Get started** if Authentication is not initialized yet.
2. Go to **Sign-in method**.
3. Open **Anonymous**.
4. Toggle **Enable**.

>
> One more pass: I’m checking the Firebase rules, because a hosted app with anonymous sign-in can look private while being effectively writable by any visitor.
</details>

**Findings**
1. **Critical: public anonymous users can read and write the whole database.**
The app signs everyone in anonymously, and Firestore/Storage rules allow any signed-in user to read/write everything. That means anyone with the hosted link could change loans, sales, customers, uploads, and snapshots. See [main.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/main.dart:12), [firestore.rules](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/firestore.rules:9), [storage.rules](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/storage.rules:9).

2. **High: money-changing writes can overwrite each other.**
`batchUpdate()` reads the latest sheet snapshot, edits it in memory, then writes the whole payload back. Two staff members saving at the same time can lose one person’s update. New pawn row numbers are also based on current list length. See [pawntrack_api.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/services/pawntrack_api.dart:36), [pawntrack_api.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/services/pawntrack_api.dart:146), [pawntrack_app.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/screens/pawntrack_app.dart:121).

3. **High: dashboard cash/profit numbers are misleading.**
“Cash collected today” is calculated from loans whose `dateGiven` is today, not repayments made today. “Profit forecast” adds sales earned and inventory value, which is not real profit. See [operating_screens.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/screens/operating_screens.dart:719), [pawntrack_models.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/models/pawntrack_models.dart:263).

4. **High: the app says Google Sheets is live, but hosted writes are Firestore-only.**
The UI says “Live Google Sheets connected,” while writes create `syncJobs` with `status: firestore_only`. That is dangerous because staff may think the Sheet is updated when it is not. See [pawntrack_app.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/screens/pawntrack_app.dart:70), [pawntrack_api.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/services/pawntrack_api.dart:159).

5. **Medium: Gemini receives customer operational data from the client.**
The prompt includes loan rows, phone numbers, overdue status, balances, and inventory data. That may be acceptable later, but it needs explicit privacy handling and staff auth first. See [pawntrack_ai_service.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/services/pawntrack_ai_service.dart:41).

**Agent 1: Normal User**
The app feels much closer to a daily pawnshop tool now. Home shows the right things: due today, overdue, repayments, sales, reminders, and Voice Command. The biggest user problem is trust: labels like “Live Google Sheets connected,” “Cash collected today,” and “Profit forecast” sound official, but some are not truly what they say yet. For a shop worker, wrong cash numbers are worse than missing charts.

**Agent 2: Experienced Programmer**
The Flutter code is clean enough and `dart analyze` passes with no issues. The main architectural problem is that the app is now doing direct Firestore business writes from the client, while still using a sheet-shaped snapshot as the central record. That is okay for a prototype, but not safe for real pawnshop transactions. Move money-changing operations to proper Firestore documents/transactions, add staff auth/roles, and make Google Sheets sync explicit.

**Agent 3: UI Specialist**
The screen direction is good: daily command centre first, charts pushed back, primary actions visible. The UI still needs sharper operational hierarchy. “Voice Command” opens an “Ask Gemini” text panel, which is useful, but it should feel like one coherent assistant action. Also, cards need confidence labels: “Synced to Firestore,” “Pending Google Sheets sync,” “Estimated profit,” “Actual profit.” That would prevent staff from treating estimates as final business records.

**Verification**
I used the Graphify project graph, inspected the Flutter source, and ran `dart analyze lib`: no analyzer issues found.

**Finding 2: Writes Can Overwrite Each Other**
Path: [pawntrack_api.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/services/pawntrack_api.dart:36)
Path: [pawntrack_app.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/screens/pawntrack_app.dart:121)

Options:
1. **Good quick fix:** use Firestore transactions around `sheetSnapshots/latest`.
   This reduces lost updates while keeping the current app structure.
2. **Better fix:** stop using list length for new pawn row numbers and create Firestore document IDs first.
   Then mirror the row-style snapshot after the fact.
3. **Best fix:** make `loans`, `repayments`, `inventory`, and `sales` the real write targets.
   Build `sheetSnapshots/latest` as a read model instead of treating it as the main editable record.

Recommended now: option 1 plus option 2.

**Finding 3: Cash/Profit Numbers Are Misleading**
Path: [operating_screens.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/screens/operating_screens.dart:64)
Path: [operating_screens.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/screens/operating_screens.dart:719)
Path: [pawntrack_models.dart](./pawntrack-flutter-port/app/lib/models/pawntrack_models.dart:263)

Options:
1. **Rename honestly:** change “Cash collected today” to “Recorded paid amount” if repayment dates are missing.
2. **Track real repayments:** use the `repayments` collection with timestamps and calculate today’s cash from repayment records.
3. **Split profit cards:** show “Actual profit from sold items” and “Estimated inventory value” separately.
4. **Change forecast formula:** profit forecast should not count full inventory value as profit.

Recommended now: option 2, option 3, and option 4.

Options:

> # Add Firebase Email Login and Settings Logout
>
> ## Summary
> Add a login screen before the PawnTrack dashboard. Remove the current anonymous sign-in flow from the app startup. Users will sign in with Firebase Email/Password accounts that are created manually in Firebase Console. Firebase Auth will keep the user signed in across refreshes. The existing “Sync” tab will become a proper “Settings” menu that shows the signed-in user and provides a logout button.
>
> ## Key Changes
> - Replace anonymous startup auth in `lib/main.dart`.
>   - Remove `FirebaseAuth.instance.signInAnonymously()`.
>   - Initialize Firebase, then run a root `MaterialApp` with an auth gate.
>   - The auth gate listens to `FirebaseAuth.instance.authStateChanges()`.
>   - If no user is signed in, show the login screen.
>   - If a user is signed in, show the PawnTrack dashboard.
>
> - Add a new login screen.
>   - New file: `lib/screens/login_screen.dart`.
>   - Fields: email and password.
>   - Button: `Login`.
>   - Uses `FirebaseAuth.instance.signInWithEmailAndPassword(email, password)`.
>   - No in-app signup, because users are created manually.
>   - Show clear errors for wrong password, user not found, invalid email, disabled user, and network failure.
>   - Disable the login button while signing in.
>   - Keep the visual style aligned with the existing app: Last Resort Pawnshop title, simple centered form, no marketing page.
>
> - Add an auth gate/root wrapper.
>   - New file: `lib/screens/auth_gate.dart` or equivalent small root widget.
>   - Shows a loading indicator while Firebase restores the saved session.
>   - Uses Firebase Auth’s normal persistence so users stay logged in after refresh or reopening the app.
>   - On web, explicitly use local persistence if supported by the installed `firebase_auth` package.
>
> - Refactor the dashboard shell enough to accept the current user.
>   - Update `PawnTrackApp` to receive:
>     - `User currentUser`
>     - `Future<void> Function() onLogout`
>   - Move the `MaterialApp` wrapper to the new root so login and dashboard share the same theme.
>   - Keep all existing dashboard tabs and data behavior unchanged.
>
> - Turn the existing Sync tab into Settings.
>   - In `lib/screens/pawntrack_app.dart`, rename the last nav item from `Sync` to `Settings`.
>   - Change icon from sync-only to settings-style.
>   - Pass `currentUser` and `onLogout` into `SyncSettingsScreen`.
>
> - Update Settings screen.
>   - In `lib/screens/operating_screens.dart`, update `SyncSettingsScreen`.
>   - Title: `Settings`.
>   - Include a `Current User` panel showing:
>     - email
>     - display name if present
>     - Firebase UID
>     - email verified status
>     - account creation time if available
>     - last sign-in time if available
>   - Add a `Logout` button.
>   - On click, call `FirebaseAuth.instance.signOut()` via the `onLogout` callback.
>   - After logout, auth gate automatically returns to login screen.
>   - Keep the existing sync status panel below the user panel.
>
> ## Firebase Console Requirements
> - Enable Firebase Authentication Email/Password provider for project `lastresort-2b8b1`.
> - Manually create staff users in Firebase Console.
> - Do not enable in-app registration.
> - Existing Firestore rules can remain `request.auth != null` for now.
> - Known future security item: anonymous/public access should be removed from Firebase Console when the login rollout is ready.
>
> ## Test Plan
> - Run `dart analyze lib`.
> - Launch app locally.
> - Signed-out state:
>   - App opens to login screen, not dashboard.
>   - Dashboard data is not visible before login.
>   - Bad password shows a readable error.
>   - Unknown email shows a readable error.
> - Signed-in state:
>   - Valid Firebase email/password opens the dashboard.
>   - Refreshing the browser keeps the user logged in.
>   - Closing and reopening the app keeps the user logged in.
>   - Dashboard data still loads from Firestore.
> - Settings:
>   - Settings tab appears in navigation.
>   - Current user email and UID display correctly.
>   - Logout returns to login screen.
>   - After logout, dashboard is no longer visible.
> - Regression:
>   - Voice Command / Gemini panel still opens.
>   - Firestore reads still work for signed-in users.
>   - Existing New Pawn, Repayment, Sales, Reports, and Settings screens still compile.
>
> ## Assumptions
> - Users will be created manually in Firebase Console.
> - No password reset screen is required in this pass.
> - No role-based permissions are required yet.
> - Anonymous Auth may still be enabled in Firebase Console temporarily, but the app will stop signing in anonymously.
> - The current Firestore rule of “signed-in users can read/write” remains acceptable until role-based security is added.
